â”‚  WHY MICROSERVICES ARE HARD:                                                â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Distributed systems are inherently complex                               â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Network is unreliable (fallacies of distributed computing)               â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Data consistency across services is challenging                          â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Operational overhead is significant                                      â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Debugging distributed issues is difficult                                â”‚
â”‚                                                                             â”‚
â”‚  KEY OPTIMIZATION TIPS:                                                     â”‚
â”‚  âœ“ Start with a modular monolith, extract when needed                       â”‚
â”‚  âœ“ Define service boundaries using Domain-Driven Design                     â”‚
â”‚  âœ“ Prefer async communication for loose coupling                            â”‚
â”‚  âœ“ Embrace eventual consistency where possible                              â”‚
â”‚  âœ“ Design for failure from the start                                        â”‚
â”‚  âœ“ Invest heavily in observability                                          â”‚
â”‚  âœ“ Automate everything (CI/CD, infrastructure)                              â”‚
â”‚  âœ“ Keep services small but not too small (avoid nanoservices)               â”‚
â”‚                                                                             â”‚
â”‚  PREREQUISITES FOR SUCCESS:                                                 â”‚
â”‚  â–¡ Mature DevOps practices and culture                                      â”‚
â”‚  â–¡ Strong automated testing capabilities                                    â”‚
â”‚  â–¡ Container orchestration platform (Kubernetes)                            â”‚
â”‚  â–¡ Centralized logging and monitoring                                       â”‚
â”‚  â–¡ CI/CD pipelines per service                                              â”‚
â”‚  â–¡ Team autonomy and clear ownership                                        â”‚

â”Œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”

â”‚   â€¢ Does one thing well                                         â”‚
â”‚   â€¢ Focused on a single business capability                     â”‚
â”‚   â€¢ Can be described in one sentence                            â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   2. INDEPENDENTLY DEPLOYABLE                                   â”‚
â”‚   â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€                                   â”‚
â”‚   â€¢ Deploy without coordinating with other services             â”‚
â”‚   â€¢ Own release schedule                                        â”‚
â”‚   â€¢ Changes don't require other services to change              â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   3. OWNS ITS DATA                                              â”‚
â”‚   â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€                                          â”‚
â”‚   â€¢ Has its own database/schema                                 â”‚
â”‚   â€¢ No shared database with other services                      â”‚
â”‚   â€¢ Data accessed only through service API                      â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   4. COMMUNICATES VIA WELL-DEFINED APIS                         â”‚
â”‚   â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€                         â”‚
â”‚   â€¢ Clear contract (REST, gRPC, events)                         â”‚
â”‚   â€¢ Versioned APIs                                              â”‚
â”‚   â€¢ Technology agnostic communication                           â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   5. OWNED BY A SMALL TEAM                                      â”‚
â”‚   â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€                                    â”‚
â”‚   â€¢ "Two pizza team" (5-9 people)                               â”‚
â”‚   â€¢ Full ownership (build, deploy, operate)                     â”‚
â”‚   â€¢ Autonomous decision making                                  â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚

â”‚   â”‚   â€¢ Can't be understood in isolation                    â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚                                                         â”‚   â”‚

â”‚   â”‚   â€¢ Team can fully understand it                        â”‚   â”‚
â”‚   â”‚   â€¢ Can be rewritten in 2-4 weeks                       â”‚   â”‚

â”‚   â”‚                                                         â”‚   â”‚

â”‚   â”‚   â€¢ Team can't understand all of it                     â”‚   â”‚

The Distributed Systems Reality

â”Œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”
â”‚              FALLACIES OF DISTRIBUTED COMPUTING                  â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¤
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   These assumptions are FALSE but often made:                   â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   1. THE NETWORK IS RELIABLE                                    â”‚
â”‚      Reality: Networks fail, packets get lost                   â”‚
â”‚      Impact: Need retry logic, circuit breakers                 â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   2. LATENCY IS ZERO                                            â”‚
â”‚      Reality: Network calls take time (ms to seconds)           â”‚
â”‚      Impact: Can't treat remote calls like local calls          â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   3. BANDWIDTH IS INFINITE                                      â”‚
â”‚      Reality: Network capacity is limited                       â”‚
â”‚      Impact: Need to minimize data transfer                     â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   4. THE NETWORK IS SECURE                                      â”‚
â”‚      Reality: Networks can be compromised                       â”‚
â”‚      Impact: Need encryption, authentication                    â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   5. TOPOLOGY DOESN'T CHANGE                                    â”‚
â”‚      Reality: Services move, scale, fail                        â”‚
â”‚      Impact: Need service discovery                             â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   6. THERE IS ONE ADMINISTRATOR                                 â”‚
â”‚      Reality: Multiple teams, multiple systems                  â”‚
â”‚      Impact: Need clear ownership, coordination                 â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   7. TRANSPORT COST IS ZERO                                     â”‚
â”‚      Reality: Serialization, network I/O costs                  â”‚
â”‚      Impact: Consider data locality                             â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   8. THE NETWORK IS HOMOGENEOUS                                 â”‚
â”‚      Reality: Different protocols, versions, formats            â”‚
â”‚      Impact: Need adapters, compatibility                       â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   â”Œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”   â”‚

5.2 Service Decomposition Strategies

Decomposition Approaches

â”‚   When calling multiple services, call in parallel              â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚
â”‚   âŒ Sequential (slow):                                         â”‚
â”‚   product = await productService.get()     // 100ms             â”‚

â”‚   âœ… Parallel (fast):                                           â”‚

â”‚     productService.get(),                                       â”‚
â”‚     reviewService.get(),                                        â”‚

â”‚   ])                                                            â”‚

â”‚   DEFINITION:                                                   â”‚
â”‚   A saga is a sequence of local transactions where each         â”‚
â”‚   transaction publishes events that trigger the next            â”‚
â”‚   transaction. If one fails, compensating transactions          â”‚
â”‚   undo previous steps.                                          â”‚
â”‚                                                                 â”‚

â”œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¤
â”‚                                                                                 â”‚
â”‚  WHAT IT IS:                                                                    â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ An architectural style where applications are built as a collection of       â”‚
â”‚    small, autonomous services that are independently deployable                 â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Each service owns its data and communicates via well-defined APIs            â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Services are organized around business capabilities, not technical layers    â”‚
â”‚                                                                                 â”‚
â”‚  CORE CHARACTERISTICS:                                                          â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Single Responsibility - Each service does one thing well                     â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Autonomous - Services can be developed, deployed, scaled independently       â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Decentralized - No central database, governance is distributed               â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Resilient - Failure in one service doesn't cascade to others                 â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Observable - Built-in monitoring, logging, and tracing                       â”‚
â”‚                                                                                 â”‚
â”‚  KEY OPTIMIZATION TIPS:                                                         â”‚
â”‚  âœ“ Start with a modular monolith, extract services when boundaries are clear   â”‚
â”‚  âœ“ Use Domain-Driven Design to identify service boundaries                      â”‚
â”‚  âœ“ Implement the Strangler Fig pattern for gradual migration                    â”‚
â”‚  âœ“ Design for failure - assume any service can fail at any time                 â”‚
â”‚  âœ“ Invest heavily in observability from day one                                 â”‚
â”‚  âœ“ Automate everything - testing, deployment, infrastructure                    â”‚
â”‚  âœ“ Keep services small but not too small (avoid nano-services)                  â”‚
â”‚  âœ“ Use asynchronous communication where possible for loose coupling             â”‚
â”‚                                                                                 â”‚
â”‚  WHEN TO USE MICROSERVICES:                                                     â”‚
â”‚  âœ“ Large teams that need to work independently                                  â”‚
â”‚  âœ“ Different parts of the system have different scaling requirements            â”‚
â”‚  âœ“ Need for technology diversity (different languages/frameworks)               â”‚
â”‚  âœ“ Rapid, independent deployment of features is critical                        â”‚
â”‚  âœ“ Organization structure supports distributed ownership                        â”‚
â”‚                                                                                 â”‚
â”‚  WHEN TO AVOID MICROSERVICES:                                                   â”‚
â”‚  âœ— Small team (< 10 developers)                                                 â”‚
â”‚  âœ— Simple domain with unclear boundaries                                        â”‚
â”‚  âœ— Limited DevOps maturity                                                      â”‚
â”‚  âœ— Tight coupling between components is unavoidable                             â”‚
â”‚  âœ— Strong consistency requirements across the system                            â”‚
â”‚                                                                                 â”‚

Detailed Comparison Matrix

AspectMonolithMicroservices
DeploymentSingle unit, all-or-nothingIndependent per service
ScalingScale entire applicationScale individual services
TechnologySingle tech stackPolyglot (multiple technologies)
Data ManagementSingle shared databaseDatabase per service
Team StructureFeature teams work on same codebaseTeams own specific services
ComplexityIn the codeIn the infrastructure
ConsistencyEasy (ACID transactions)Hard (eventual consistency)
DebuggingSingle process, easierDistributed tracing needed
LatencyIn-process callsNetwork calls add latency
Initial DevelopmentFasterSlower (infrastructure overhead)
Long-term MaintenanceCan become difficultEasier with clear boundaries

â”‚  SAMPLING STRATEGIES:                                                           â”‚
â”‚  â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€                                                           â”‚
â”‚  Tracing everything is expensive - use sampling                                 â”‚
â”‚                                                                                 â”‚
â”‚  1. HEAD-BASED SAMPLING                                                         â”‚
â”‚     Decision made at start of trace                                             â”‚
â”‚     Example: Sample 10% of all traces                                           â”‚
â”‚     Pro: Simple, predictable cost                                               â”‚
â”‚     Con: Might miss interesting traces                                          â”‚
â”‚                                                                                 â”‚
â”‚  2. TAIL-BASED SAMPLING                                                         â”‚
â”‚     Decision made at end of trace                                               â”‚
â”‚     Example: Keep traces with errors or high latency                            â”‚
â”‚     Pro: Captures interesting traces                                            â”‚
â”‚     Con: More complex, higher memory usage                                      â”‚
â”‚                                                                                 â”‚
â”‚  3. ADAPTIVE SAMPLING                                                           â”‚
â”‚     Adjust rate based on traffic                                                â”‚
â”‚     Example: Sample more during low traffic, less during high                   â”‚
â”‚                                                                                 â”‚
â”‚  POPULAR TRACING TOOLS:                                                         â”‚
